{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /app/.claude/skills/data_cleaning\n\n# Guidance\n\n## Decision Framework\n\n**Deduplication**: Check for duplicates first. Examine logical structure and downstream goals:\n- Survey/demographic data: one row per respondent (remove duplicate IDs)\n- Transaction data: multiple transactions per user are legitimate (do NOT deduplicate by user alone)\n- Use appropriate subset of columns that define uniqueness\n\n**Missing Value Strategy**:\n1. Critical columns (IDs, dates, outcome variables): drop rows with missingness\n2. Non-critical numerical: impute with median\n3. Non-critical categorical: impute with mode\n4. Non-critical with strong relationships to other columns: consider KNN imputation\n\n**Outlier Handling**:\n- If sample size is large and outliers are clearly errors: remove using IQR or Z-score\n- If sample size is precious or outliers might be real: cap using winsorization\n- Default: 1.5 for IQR multiplier, 3.0 for Z-score\n- For causal inference: be cautious about removing extreme values\n\n## Implementation Pattern\n\n1. Read and preview data (`df.head()`, `df.info()`, `df.describe()`)\n2. Check for duplicates and understand their source\n3. Identify missing value patterns (`df.isnull().sum()`)\n4. Clean in stages: identifiers → critical fields → non-critical fields → outliers\n5. Verify referential integrity between related datasets\n6. Document rows affected by each operation\n7. Save cleaned outputs with clear naming\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n**Survey/Demographic Data**:\n- Expect one row per respondent\n- Remove duplicate Survey ResponseIDs\n- Demographic columns may need imputation\n- Verify IDs follow expected format\n\n**Transaction/Purchase Data**:\n- Multiple transactions per user are normal\n- Date columns must be parseable and within expected range\n- Price/amount should be positive and within reasonable bounds\n- Category columns should not have nulls\n- Verify Survey ResponseIDs link to demographic data\n\n**Cross-Dataset Validation**:\n- After cleaning, verify transaction IDs exist in demographic data\n- Filter transactions to only include users in cleaned demographics if required\n- Ensure date ranges align with analysis requirements\n\n# Execution Notes\n\n1. **Always preview before cleaning**: Use `df.head()`, `df.info()`, `df.describe()` to understand data structure before applying operations\n\n2. **Document decisions**: Note why you chose each approach (e.g., \"Dropping rows with missing Category because required for aggregation\")\n\n3. **Check referential integrity early**: Verify IDs in transaction data exist in demographic data before proceeding\n\n4. **Be conservative with outlier removal**: For causal inference, extreme values may represent real effects. Configuration:\")\n\n# Input/output paths\noutput_dir = Path('/app/output')\npurchase_path = output_dir / 'amazon-purchases-2019-2020-filtered.csv'\n\n# Time windows\ncutoff_date = '2020-03-01'  # Training uses data before this\nprediction_start = '2020-03-01'\nprediction_end = '2020-03-31'\nbaseline_start = '2020-01-01'\nbaseline_end = '2020-02-29'\n\n# Prophet parameters\nmin_training_days = 180\nconfidence_interval = 0.68  # ±1 sigma\nchangepoint_prior_scale = 0.1\nseasonality_prior_scale = 10.0\n\nprint(f\"   Training cutoff: {cutoff_date}\")\nprint(f\"   Prediction window: {prediction_start} to {prediction_end}\")\nprint(f\"   Baseline window: {baseline_start} to {baseline_end}\")\nprint(f\"   Min training days: {min_training_days}\")\nprint(f\"   Confidence interval: {confidence_interval}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# LOAD AND AGGREGATE DATA\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n2. Loading and aggregating transaction data:\")\n\n# Load cleaned purchase data\npurchase_df = pd.read_csv(purchase_path)\npurchase_df['Order Date'] = pd.to_datetime(purchase_df['Order Date'])\nprint(f\"   Total transactions: {len(purchase_df)}\")\nprint(f\"   Date range: {purchase_df['Order Date'].min().date()} to {purchase_df['Order Date'].max().date()}\")\nprint(f\"   Unique categories: {purchase_df['Category'].nunique()}\")\n\n# Calculate total spend per transaction\npurchase_df['Total_Spend'] = purchase_df['Purchase Price Per Unit'] * purchase_df['Quantity']\n\n# Aggregate to daily category level\nprint(\"\\n3. Aggregating to daily category-level time series:\")\ndaily_category = purchase_df.groupby(['Order Date', 'Category']).agg({\n    'Total_Spend': 'sum',\n    'Survey ResponseID': 'nunique'\n}).reset_index()\ndaily_category.columns = ['ds', 'Category', 'y', 'n_purchasers']\n\nprint(f\"   Daily category records: {len(daily_category)}\")\nprint(f\"   Categories with transactions: {daily_category['Category'].nunique()}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# FILTER CATEGORIES BY MINIMUM TRAINING DATA\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n4. Filtering categories by minimum training days:\")\n\n# Split data for counting training days\ntraining_data = daily_category[daily_category['ds'] < cutoff_date].copy()\n\n# Count training days per category\ncategory_training_days = training_data.groupby('Category')['ds'].count()\nvalid_categories = category_training_days[category_training_days >= min_training_days].index.tolist()\n\nprint(f\"   Categories meeting min training days ({min_training_days}): {len(valid_categories)}\")\nprint(f\"   Categories filtered out: {purchase_df['Category'].nunique() - len(valid_categories)}\")\n\nif len(valid_categories) < 20:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Only {len(valid_categories)} categories have sufficient data\")\n    print(f\"   Adjusting minimum training days to get more categories...\")\n\n    # Gradually reduce threshold to get at least 20 categories\n    for new_threshold in [150, 120, 90, 60, 30]:\n        valid_categories = category_training_days[category_training_days >= new_threshold].index.tolist()\n        if len(valid_categories) >= 20:\n            min_training_days = new_threshold\n            print(f\"   Using {new_threshold} days threshold: {len(valid_categories)} categories\")\n            break\n\n# Filter to valid categories only\ndaily_category = daily_category[daily_category['Category'].isin(valid_categories)].copy()\n\n# ============================================================================\n# RUN PROPHET FOR EACH CATEGORY\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Running Prophet models for each category:\")\nprint(f\"   Processing {len(valid_categories)} categories...\")\n\nresults = []\nerrors = []\n\nfor idx, category in enumerate(valid_categories, 1):\n    if idx % 20 == 0 or idx == len(valid_categories):\n        print(f\"   Progress: {idx}/{len(valid_categories)} categories processed\")\n\n    try:\n        # Get category data\n        cat_data = daily_category[daily_category['Category'] == category].copy()\n\n        # Training data (before cutoff)\n        train_data = cat_data[cat_data['ds'] < cutoff_date][['ds', 'y']].copy()\n\n        # Actual data for March 2020\n        actual_march = cat_data[\n            (cat_data['ds'] >= prediction_start) &\n            (cat_data['ds'] <= prediction_end)\n        ].copy()\n\n        # Actual data for baseline (Jan-Feb 2020)\n        actual_baseline = cat_data[\n            (cat_data['ds'] >= baseline_start) &\n            (cat_data['ds'] <= baseline_end)\n        ].copy()\n\n        # Skip if no training data\n        if len(train_data) < min_training_days:\n            continue\n\n        # Initialize and fit Prophet model\n        model = Prophet(\n            interval_width=confidence_interval,\n            changepoint_prior_scale=changepoint_prior_scale,\n            seasonality_prior_scale=seasonality_prior_scale,\n            daily_seasonality=False,\n            weekly_seasonality=True,\n            yearly_seasonality=True\n        )\n\n        # Suppress Prophet output\n        import logging\n        logging.getLogger('prophet').setLevel(logging.WARNING)\n        logging.getLogger('cmdstanpy').setLevel(logging.WARNING)\n\n        model.fit(train_data)\n\n        # Create future dataframe for prediction period\n        future_dates = pd.date_range(start=prediction_start, end=prediction_end, freq='D')\n        future_df = pd.DataFrame({'ds': future_dates})\n\n        # Generate predictions\n        forecast = model.predict(future_df)\n\n        # Calculate metrics for March 2020\n        actual_march_avg = actual_march['y'].mean() if len(actual_march) > 0 else 0\n        predicted_march_avg = forecast['yhat'].mean()\n        upper_bound_avg = forecast['yhat_upper'].mean()\n        lower_bound_avg = forecast['yhat_lower'].mean()\n\n        # Calculate metrics for baseline\n        baseline_avg = actual_baseline['y'].mean() if len(actual_baseline) > 0 else 0\n\n        # Calculate anomaly index\n        # If actual is within CI, index = 0\n        # If above upper bound: positive anomaly (surge)\n        # If below lower bound: negative anomaly (slump)\n\n        if actual_march_avg > upper_bound_avg:\n            # Surge\n            deviation = actual_march_avg - upper_bound_avg\n            std_estimate = (upper_bound_avg - predicted_march_avg) / 1.0  # 1 sigma for 68% CI\n            if std_estimate > 0:\n                raw_index = deviation / std_estimate\n            else:\n                raw_index = 0\n        elif actual_march_avg < lower_bound_avg:\n            # Loading cleaned survey data:\")\n\noutput_dir = Path('/app/output')\nsurvey_path = output_dir / 'survey_cleaned.csv'\nsurvey_df = pd.read_csv(survey_path)\n\nprint(f\"   Rows: {len(survey_df)}\")\nprint(f\"   Columns: {len(survey_df.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Survey ResponseIDs: {survey_df['Survey ResponseID'].nunique()}\")\n\n# Preview data\nprint(\"\\n   Column names:\")\nfor col in survey_df.columns:\n    print(f\"   - {col}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# SEPARATE ID FROM FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n2. Separating Survey ResponseID from features:\")\n\nresponse_id = survey_df['Survey ResponseID'].copy()\ndemo_features = survey_df.drop('Survey ResponseID', axis=1).copy()\n\nprint(f\"   Features to engineer: {len(demo_features.columns)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# DEFINE FEATURE TRANSFORMATIONS\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n3. Categorizing features by type:\")\n\n# Binary features (Yes/No)\nbinary_simple = [\n    'Q-demos-hispanic',\n    'Q-personal-diabetes',\n    'Q-personal-wheelchair'\n]\n\n# Substance use features (Yes/No/Prefer not to say/I stopped...)\nsubstance_features = [\n    'Q-substance-use-cigarettes',\n    'Q-substance-use-marijuana',\n    'Q-substance-use-alcohol'\n]\n\n# Ordinal features (with natural ordering)\nordinal_features = {\n    'Q-demos-age': [\n        '18 - 24 years',\n        '25 - 34 years',\n        '35 - 44 years',\n        '45 - 54 years',\n        '55 - 64 years',\n        '65 and older'\n    ],\n    'Q-demos-education': [\n        'Some high school or less',\n        'High school diploma or GED',\n        'Some college but no degree',\n        'Associate\\'s degree',\n        'Bachelor\\'s degree',\n        'Graduate or professional degree (MA, MS, MBA, PhD, JD, MD, DDS, etc)'\n    ],\n    'Q-demos-income': [\n        'Less than $25,000',\n        '$25,000 - $49,999',\n        '$50,000 - $74,999',\n        '$75,000 - $99,999',\n        '$100,000 - $149,999',\n        '$150,000 or more',\n        'Prefer not to say'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-howmany': [\n        '1 (just me!)',\n        '2',\n        '3',\n        '4+'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-hh-size': [\n        '1 (just me!)',\n        '2',\n        '3',\n        '4+'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-how-oft': [\n        'Less than 5 times per month',\n        '5 - 10 times per month',\n        'More than 10 times per month'\n    ]\n}\n\n# Nominal features (no natural order - one-hot encode)\nnominal_features = [\n    'Q-demos-race',\n    'Q-demos-gender',\n    'Q-sexual-orientation',\n    'Q-demos-state'\n]\n\nprint(f\"   Binary (simple Yes/No): {len(binary_simple)}\")\nprint(f\"   Substance use (multi-level): {len(substance_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Ordinal: {len(ordinal_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Nominal: {len(nominal_features)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM BINARY FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n4. Transforming binary features:\")\n\nfor col in binary_simple:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Map Yes to 1, No to 0\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].map({'Yes': 1, 'No': 0})\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].astype(int)\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: Yes/No → 1/0\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM SUBSTANCE USE FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Transforming substance use features:\")\n\nfor col in substance_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Check unique values\n        unique_vals = demo_features[col].unique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {len(unique_vals)} unique values\")\n\n        # Create binary: currently using (Yes) vs not currently using\n        demo_features[f'{col}_current'] = (demo_features[col] == 'Yes').astype(int)\n\n        # Create binary: ever used (Yes or stopped)\n        demo_features[f'{col}_ever'] = (\n            (demo_features[col] == 'Yes') |\n            (demo_features[col] == 'I stopped in the recent past')\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Create prefer not to say indicator\n        demo_features[f'{col}_undisclosed'] = (\n            demo_features[col] == 'Prefer not to say'\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Drop original column\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created: {col}_current, {col}_ever, {col}_undisclosed\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM ORDINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Transforming ordinal features:\")\n\nfor col, order in ordinal_features.items():\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Create ordered categorical\n        demo_features[col] = pd.Categorical(\n            demo_features[col],\n            categories=order,\n            ordered=True\n        )\n\n        # Convert to codes (0, 1, 2, ...)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].codes\n\n        # Handle any -1 (missing category) - shouldn't happen after cleaning\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].replace(-1, 0)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: encoded as ordinal (0-{len(order)-1})\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# ONE-HOT ENCODE NOMINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n7. One-hot encoding nominal features:\")\n\nfor col in nominal_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        unique_count = demo_features[col].nunique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {unique_count} unique values\")\n\n        # One-hot encode\n        dummies = pd.get_dummies(demo_features[col], prefix=col, drop_first=False)\n\n        # Drop original column and add dummies\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        demo_features = pd.concat([demo_features, dummies], axis=1)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created {len(dummies.columns)} one-hot features\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# VALIDATE ALL FEATURES ARE NUMERIC\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n8. Validating feature transformations:\")\n\n# Check data types\nnon_numeric_cols = []\nfor col in demo_features.columns:\n    if demo_features[col].dtype not in ['int64', 'float64', 'int32', 'float32']:\n        non_numeric_cols.append(col)\n\nif len(non_numeric_cols) > 0:\n    print(f\"   ERROR: Found non-numeric columns: {non_numeric_cols}\")\n    for col in non_numeric_cols:\n        print(f\"   - {col}: {demo_features[col].dtype}\")\n        print(f\"     Sample values: {demo_features[col].head().tolist()}\")\n    raise ValueError(\"All features must be numeric!\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ All {len(demo_features.columns)} features are numeric\")\n\n# Check for missing values\nmissing_counts = demo_features.isnull().sum()\nif missing_counts.sum() > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found missing values:\")\n    for col, count in missing_counts[missing_counts > 0].items():\n        print(f\"   - {col}: {count}\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ No missing values\")\n\n# Check for constant features\nconstant_features = []\nfor col in demo_features.columns:\n    if demo_features[col].nunique() == 1:\n        constant_features.append(col)\n\nif len(constant_features) > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found {len(constant_features)} constant features (will be removed):\")\n    for col in constant_features[:5]:\n        print(f\"   - {col}\")\n    # Remove constant features\n    demo_features = demo_features.drop(constant_features, axis=1)\n    print(f\"   ✓ Removed {len(constant_features)} constant features\")\n\n# Check for infinite values\ninfinite_counts = np.isinf(demo_features.select_dtypes(include=[np.number])).sum()\nif infinite_counts.sum() > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found infinite values\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ No infinite values\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# COMBINE AND SAVE\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n9. Creating final output:\")\n\n# Combine Survey ResponseID with engineered features\noutput_df = pd.concat([response_id.reset_index(drop=True),\n                       demo_features.reset_index(drop=True)], axis=1)\n\nprint(f\"   Total columns: {len(output_df.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Survey ResponseID column: 1\")\nprint(f\"   Feature columns: {len(demo_features.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Total rows: {len(output_df)}\")\n\n# Final validation\nfeature_cols = [c for c in output_df.columns if c != 'Survey ResponseID']\nnumeric_cols = output_df[feature_cols].select_dtypes(include=['int64', 'float64', 'int32', 'float32']).columns\nprint(f\"\\n   Final validation:\")\nprint(f\"   - Feature count: {len(feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Numeric features: {len(numeric_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - All numeric: {len(feature_cols) == len(numeric_cols)}\")\n\n# Save output\noutput_path = output_dir / 'survey_feature_engineered.csv'\noutput_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {output_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# SUMMARY STATISTICS\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n10. Feature summary:\")\n\nprint(f\"\\n   Sample feature names (first 20):\")\nfor i, col in enumerate(feature_cols[:20], 1):\n    print(f\"   {i:2d}. {col}\")\n\nif len(feature_cols) > 20:\n    print(f\"   ... and {len(feature_cols) - 20} more features\")\n\nprint(f\"\\n   Feature statistics:\")\nprint(f\"   - Total features: {len(feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Binary features (0/1): {sum(output_df[col].nunique() == 2 for col in feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Multi-level features: {sum(output_df[col].nunique() > 2 for col in feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Min unique values: {min(output_df[col].nunique() for col in feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Max unique values: {max(output_df[col].nunique() for col in feature_cols)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# FINAL SUMMARY\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n\" + \"=\"*80)\nprint(\"FEATURE ENGINEERING COMPLETE - SUMMARY\")\nprint(\"=\"*80)\n\nprint(f\"\\nINPUT:\")\nprint(f\"  - Cleaned survey data: {len(survey_df)} respondents\")\nprint(f\"  - Original demographic columns: {len(survey_df.columns) - 1}\")\n\nprint(f\"\\nOUTPUT:\")\nprint(f\"  - Transforming binary features:\")\n\nfor col in binary_simple:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Map Yes to 1, No to 0\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].map({'Yes': 1, 'No': 0})\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].astype(int)\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: Yes/No → 1/0\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM SUBSTANCE USE FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Transforming substance use features:\")\n\nfor col in substance_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Check unique values\n        unique_vals = demo_features[col].unique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {len(unique_vals)} unique values\")\n\n        # Create binary: currently using (Yes) vs not currently using\n        demo_features[f'{col}_current'] = (demo_features[col] == 'Yes').astype(int)\n\n        # Create binary: ever used (Yes or stopped)\n        demo_features[f'{col}_ever'] = (\n            (demo_features[col] == 'Yes') |\n            (demo_features[col] == 'I stopped in the recent past')\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Create prefer not to say indicator\n        demo_features[f'{col}_undisclosed'] = (\n            demo_features[col] == 'Prefer not to say'\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Drop original column\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created: {col}_current, {col}_ever, {col}_undisclosed\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM ORDINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Transforming ordinal features:\")\n\nfor col, order in ordinal_features.items():\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Create ordered categorical\n        demo_features[col] = pd.Categorical(\n            demo_features[col],\n            categories=order,\n            ordered=True\n        )\n\n        # Convert to codes (0, 1, 2, ...)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].codes\n\n        # Handle any -1 (missing category) - shouldn't happen after cleaning\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].replace(-1, 0)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: encoded as ordinal (0-{len(order)-1})\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# ONE-HOT ENCODE NOMINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n7. One-hot encoding nominal features:\")\n\nfor col in nominal_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        unique_count = demo_features[col].nunique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {unique_count} unique values\")\n\n        # One-hot encode\n        dummies = pd.get_dummies(demo_features[col], prefix=col, drop_first=False)\n\n        # Drop original column and add dummies\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        demo_features = pd.concat([demo_features, dummies], axis=1)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created {len(dummies.columns)} one-hot features\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# VALIDATE ALL FEATURES ARE NUMERIC\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n8. Validating feature transformations:\")\n\n# Check data types\nnon_numeric_cols = []\nfor col in demo_features.columns:\n    if demo_features[col].dtype not in ['int64', 'float64', 'int32', 'float32']:\n        non_numeric_cols.append(col)\n\nif len(non_numeric_cols) > 0:\n    print(f\"   ERROR: Found non-numeric columns: {non_numeric_cols}\")\n    for col in non_numeric_cols:\n        print(f\"   - {col}: {demo_features[col].dtype}\")\n        print(f\"     Sample values: {demo_features[col].head().tolist()}\")\n    raise ValueError(\"All features must be numeric!\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ All {len(demo_features.columns)} features are numeric\")\n\n# Check for missing values\nmissing_counts = demo_features.isnull().sum()\nif missing_counts.sum() > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found missing values:\")\n    for col, count in missing_counts[missing_counts > 0].items():\n        print(f\"   - {col}: {count}\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ No missing values\")\n\n# Check for constant features\nconstant_features = []\nfor col in demo_features.columns:\n    if demo_features[col].nunique() == 1:\n        constant_features.append(col)\n\nif len(constant_features) > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found {len(constant_features)} constant features (will be removed):\")\n    for col in constant_features[:5]:\n        print(f\"   - {col}\")\n    # Remove constant features\n    demo_features = demo_features.drop(constant_features, axis=1)\n    print(f\"   ✓ Removed {len(constant_features)} constant features\")\n\n# Check for infinite values\ninfinite_counts = np.isinf(demo_features.select_dtypes(include=[np.number])).sum()\nif infinite_counts.sum() > 0:\n    print(f\"   WARNING: Found infinite values\")\nelse:\n    print(f\"   ✓ No infinite values\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# COMBINE AND SAVE\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n9. Creating final output:\")\n\n# Combine Survey ResponseID with engineered features\noutput_df = pd.concat([response_id.reset_index(drop=True),\n                       demo_features.reset_index(drop=True)], axis=1)\n\nprint(f\"   Total columns: {len(output_df.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Survey ResponseID column: 1\")\nprint(f\"   Feature columns: {len(demo_features.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Total rows: {len(output_df)}\")\n\n# Final validation\nfeature_cols = [c for c in output_df.columns if c != 'Survey ResponseID']\nnumeric_cols = output_df[feature_cols].select_dtypes(include=['int64', 'float64', 'int32', 'float32']).columns\nprint(f\"\\n   Final validation:\")\nprint(f\"   - Feature count: {len(feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Numeric features: {len(numeric_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - All numeric: {len(feature_cols) == len(numeric_cols)}\")\n\n# Save output\noutput_path = output_dir / 'survey_feature_engineered.csv'\noutput_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {output_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# SUMMARY STATISTICS\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n10. Feature summary:\")\n\nprint(f\"\\n   Sample feature names (first 20):\")\nfor i, col in enumerate(feature_cols[:20], 1):\n    print(f\"   {i:2d}. {col}\")\n\nif len(feature_cols) > 20:\n    print(f\"   ... and {len(feature_cols) - 20} more features\")\n\nprint(f\"\\n   Feature statistics:\")\nprint(f\"   - Total features: {len(feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Binary features (0/1): {sum(output_df[col].nunique() == 2 for col in feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Transforming binary features:\")\n\nfor col in binary_simple:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Map Yes to 1, No to 0\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].map({'Yes': 1, 'No': 0})\n        # Fill any remaining NaN with 0 (shouldn't happen after cleaning, but safety check)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].fillna(0).astype(int)\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: Yes/No → 1/0\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM SUBSTANCE USE FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Categorizing features by type:\")\n\n# Binary features (Yes/No)\nbinary_simple = [\n    'Q-demos-hispanic',\n    'Q-personal-diabetes',\n    'Q-personal-wheelchair'\n]\n\n# Substance use features (Yes/No/Prefer not to say/I stopped...)\nsubstance_features = [\n    'Q-substance-use-cigarettes',\n    'Q-substance-use-marijuana',\n    'Q-substance-use-alcohol'\n]\n\n# Ordinal features (with natural ordering)\nordinal_features = {\n    'Q-demos-age': [\n        '18 - 24 years',\n        '25 - 34 years',\n        '35 - 44 years',\n        '45 - 54 years',\n        '55 - 64 years',\n        '65 and older'\n    ],\n    'Q-demos-education': [\n        'Some high school or less',\n        'High school diploma or GED',\n        'Some college but no degree',\n        'Associate\\'s degree',\n        'Bachelor\\'s degree',\n        'Graduate or professional degree (MA, MS, MBA, PhD, JD, MD, DDS, etc)'\n    ],\n    'Q-demos-income': [\n        'Less than $25,000',\n        '$25,000 - $49,999',\n        '$50,000 - $74,999',\n        '$75,000 - $99,999',\n        '$100,000 - $149,999',\n        '$150,000 or more',\n        'Prefer not to say'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-howmany': [\n        '1 (just me!)',\n        '2',\n        '3',\n        '4+'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-hh-size': [\n        '1 (just me!)',\n        '2',\n        '3',\n        '4+'\n    ],\n    'Q-amazon-use-how-oft': [\n        'Less than 5 times per month',\n        '5 - 10 times per month',\n        'More than 10 times per month'\n    ]\n}\n\n# Nominal features (no natural order - one-hot encode)\nnominal_features = [\n    'Q-demos-race',\n    'Q-demos-gender',\n    'Q-sexual-orientation',\n    'Q-demos-state'\n]\n\nprint(f\"   Binary (simple Yes/No): {len(binary_simple)}\")\nprint(f\"   Substance use (multi-level): {len(substance_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Ordinal: {len(ordinal_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Nominal: {len(nominal_features)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM BINARY FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n4. Transforming binary features:\")\n\nfor col in binary_simple:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Map Yes to 1, No to 0\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].map({'Yes': 1, 'No': 0})\n        # Fill any remaining NaN with 0 (shouldn't happen after cleaning, but safety check)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].fillna(0).astype(int)\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: Yes/No → 1/0\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM SUBSTANCE USE FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Transforming substance use features:\")\n\nfor col in substance_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Check unique values\n        unique_vals = demo_features[col].unique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {len(unique_vals)} unique values\")\n\n        # Create binary: currently using (Yes) vs not currently using\n        demo_features[f'{col}_current'] = (demo_features[col] == 'Yes').astype(int)\n\n        # Create binary: ever used (Yes or stopped)\n        demo_features[f'{col}_ever'] = (\n            (demo_features[col] == 'Yes') |\n            (demo_features[col] == 'I stopped in the recent past')\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Create prefer not to say indicator\n        demo_features[f'{col}_undisclosed'] = (\n            demo_features[col] == 'Prefer not to say'\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Drop original column\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created: {col}_current, {col}_ever, {col}_undisclosed\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM ORDINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Transforming ordinal features:\")\n\nfor col, order in ordinal_features.items():\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Create ordered categorical\n        demo_features[col] = pd.Categorical(\n            demo_features[col],\n            categories=order,\n            ordered=True\n        )\n\n        # Convert to codes (0, 1, 2, ...)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].cat.codes\n\n        # Handle any -1 (missing category) - shouldn't happen after cleaning\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].replace(-1, 0)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: encoded as ordinal (0-{len(order)-1})\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# ONE-HOT ENCODE NOMINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n7. One-hot encoding nominal features:\")\n\nfor col in nominal_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        unique_count = demo_features[col].nunique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {unique_count} unique values\")\n\n        # One-hot encode\n        dummies = pd.get_dummies(demo_features[col], prefix=col, drop_first=False)\n\n        # Drop original column and add dummies\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        demo_features = pd.concat([demo_features, dummies], axis=1)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created {len(dummies.columns)} one-hot features\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# VALIDATE ALL FEATURES ARE NUMERIC\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n8. Creating final output:\")\n\n# Combine Survey ResponseID with engineered features\noutput_df = pd.concat([response_id.reset_index(drop=True),\n                       demo_features.reset_index(drop=True)], axis=1)\n\nprint(f\"   Total columns: {len(output_df.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Survey ResponseID column: 1\")\nprint(f\"   Feature columns: {len(demo_features.columns)}\")\nprint(f\"   Total rows: {len(output_df)}\")\n\n# Final validation\nfeature_cols = [c for c in output_df.columns if c != 'Survey ResponseID']\nnumeric_cols = output_df[feature_cols].select_dtypes(include=['int64', 'float64', 'int32', 'float32']).columns\nprint(f\"\\n   Final validation:\")\nprint(f\"   - Feature count: {len(feature_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - Numeric features: {len(numeric_cols)}\")\nprint(f\"   - All numeric: {len(feature_cols) == len(numeric_cols)}\")\n\n# Save output\noutput_path = output_dir / 'survey_feature_engineered.csv'\noutput_df.to_csv(output_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {output_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# SUMMARY STATISTICS\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n10. 10 times per month',\n        'More than 10 times per month'\n    ]\n}\n\n# Nominal features (no natural order - one-hot encode)\nnominal_features = [\n    'Q-demos-race',\n    'Q-demos-gender',\n    'Q-sexual-orientation',\n    'Q-demos-state'\n]\n\nprint(f\"   Binary (simple Yes/No): {len(binary_simple)}\")\nprint(f\"   Substance use (multi-level): {len(substance_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Ordinal: {len(ordinal_features)}\")\nprint(f\"   Nominal: {len(nominal_features)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM BINARY FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n4. Transforming binary features:\")\n\nfor col in binary_simple:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Map Yes to 1, No to 0\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].map({'Yes': 1, 'No': 0})\n        # Fill any remaining NaN with 0 (shouldn't happen after cleaning, but safety check)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].fillna(0).astype(int)\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: Yes/No → 1/0\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM SUBSTANCE USE FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Transforming substance use features:\")\n\nfor col in substance_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Check unique values\n        unique_vals = demo_features[col].unique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {len(unique_vals)} unique values\")\n\n        # Create binary: currently using (Yes) vs not currently using\n        demo_features[f'{col}_current'] = (demo_features[col] == 'Yes').astype(int)\n\n        # Create binary: ever used (Yes or stopped)\n        demo_features[f'{col}_ever'] = (\n            (demo_features[col] == 'Yes') |\n            (demo_features[col] == 'I stopped in the recent past')\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Create prefer not to say indicator\n        demo_features[f'{col}_undisclosed'] = (\n            demo_features[col] == 'Prefer not to say'\n        ).astype(int)\n\n        # Drop original column\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created: {col}_current, {col}_ever, {col}_undisclosed\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# TRANSFORM ORDINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Transforming ordinal features:\")\n\nfor col, order in ordinal_features.items():\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        # Create ordered categorical\n        demo_features[col] = pd.Categorical(\n            demo_features[col],\n            categories=order,\n            ordered=True\n        )\n\n        # Convert to codes (0, 1, 2, ...)\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].cat.codes\n\n        # Handle any -1 (missing category) - shouldn't happen after cleaning\n        demo_features[col] = demo_features[col].replace(-1, 0)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ {col}: encoded as ordinal (0-{len(order)-1})\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# ONE-HOT ENCODE NOMINAL FEATURES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n7. One-hot encoding nominal features:\")\n\nfor col in nominal_features:\n    if col in demo_features.columns:\n        unique_count = demo_features[col].nunique()\n        print(f\"   {col}: {unique_count} unique values\")\n\n        # One-hot encode\n        dummies = pd.get_dummies(demo_features[col], prefix=col, drop_first=False)\n\n        # Drop original column and add dummies\n        demo_features = demo_features.drop(col, axis=1)\n        demo_features = pd.concat([demo_features, dummies], axis=1)\n\n        print(f\"   ✓ Created {len(dummies.columns)} one-hot features\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# VALIDATE ALL FEATURES ARE NUMERIC\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n8. Configuration:\")\n\noutput_dir = Path('/app/output')\n\n# Time periods\nbaseline_start = '2020-01-01'\nbaseline_end = '2020-02-29'\ntreatment_start = '2020-03-01'\ntreatment_end = '2020-03-31'\n\nprint(f\"   Baseline period: {baseline_start} to {baseline_end}\")\nprint(f\"   Treatment period: {treatment_start} to {treatment_end}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# LOAD DATA\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n2. Loading data:\")\n\n# Load anomaly index\nanomaly_df = pd.read_csv(output_dir / 'category_anomaly_index.csv')\nprint(f\"   Anomaly index: {len(anomaly_df)} categories\")\n\n# Load cleaned purchases\npurchase_df = pd.read_csv(output_dir / 'amazon-purchases-2019-2020-filtered.csv')\npurchase_df['Order Date'] = pd.to_datetime(purchase_df['Order Date'])\nprint(f\"   Purchases: {len(purchase_df)} transactions\")\n\n# Load engineered features\nfeatures_df = pd.read_csv(output_dir / 'survey_feature_engineered.csv')\nprint(f\"   Features: {len(features_df)} respondents, {len(features_df.columns)-1} features\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# IDENTIFY TOP SURGE AND SLUMP CATEGORIES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n3. Identifying top surge and slump categories:\")\n\n# Sort by anomaly index descending\nanomaly_df = anomaly_df.sort_values('Anomaly_Index', ascending=False).reset_index(drop=True)\n\n# Top 10 surge categories (highest positive anomaly)\ntop_surge = anomaly_df.head(10)['Category'].tolist()\nprint(f\"\\n   Top 10 SURGE categories:\")\nfor i, (idx, row) in enumerate(anomaly_df.head(10).iterrows(), 1):\n    print(f\"   {i:2d}. {row['Category']:40s} (Index: {row['Anomaly_Index']:6.2f})\")\n\n# Bottom 10 slump categories (lowest/most negative anomaly)\nbottom_slump = anomaly_df.tail(10)['Category'].tolist()\nprint(f\"\\n   Bottom 10 SLUMP categories:\")\nfor i, (idx, row) in enumerate(anomaly_df.tail(10).iloc[::-1].iterrows(), 1):\n    print(f\"   {i:2d}. {row['Category']:40s} (Index: {row['Anomaly_Index']:6.2f})\")\n\n# Combine for analysis\ntarget_categories = top_surge + bottom_slump\nprint(f\"\\n   Total target categories for DiD analysis: {len(target_categories)}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# FILTER PURCHASES TO TARGET PERIOD AND CATEGORIES\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n4. Filtering purchases to target period and categories:\")\n\n# Filter to Jan-March 2020\nperiod_purchases = purchase_df[\n    (purchase_df['Order Date'] >= baseline_start) &\n    (purchase_df['Order Date'] <= treatment_end)\n].copy()\n\nprint(f\"   Purchases in Jan-Mar 2020: {len(period_purchases)}\")\n\n# Filter to target categories\ntarget_purchases = period_purchases[\n    period_purchases['Category'].isin(target_categories)\n].copy()\n\nprint(f\"   Purchases in target categories: {len(target_purchases)}\")\n\n# Calculate total spend per transaction\ntarget_purchases['Total_Spend'] = (\n    target_purchases['Purchase Price Per Unit'] * target_purchases['Quantity']\n)\n\n# Assign period labels\ndef assign_period(date):\n    if baseline_start <= date <= baseline_end:\n        return 'baseline'\n    elif treatment_start <= date <= treatment_end:\n        return 'treatment'\n    else:\n        return 'other'\n\ntarget_purchases['Period'] = target_purchases['Order Date'].apply(\n    lambda x: assign_period(x.strftime('%Y-%m-%d'))\n)\n\n# Verify periods\nprint(f\"\\n   Purchases by period:\")\nperiod_counts = target_purchases['Period'].value_counts()\nfor period, count in period_counts.items():\n    print(f\"   - {period}: {count}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# CREATE INTENSIVE MARGIN DATA (Total_Spend)\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n5. Creating intensive margin aggregated data:\")\n\n# Aggregate total spend per user-category-period\nintensive_agg = target_purchases.groupby([\n    'Survey ResponseID',\n    'Category',\n    'Period'\n]).agg({\n    'Total_Spend': 'sum'\n}).reset_index()\n\nprint(f\"   Intensive margin records: {len(intensive_agg)}\")\nprint(f\"   Unique users: {intensive_agg['Survey ResponseID'].nunique()}\")\nprint(f\"   Unique categories: {intensive_agg['Category'].nunique()}\")\n\n# Fill in missing user-category-period combinations with 0 spend\n# First, create all possible combinations\nall_users = features_df['Survey ResponseID'].unique()\nall_periods = ['baseline', 'treatment']\n\n# Create full grid\nintensive_full = []\nfor user in all_users:\n    for category in target_categories:\n        for period in all_periods:\n            intensive_full.append({\n                'Survey ResponseID': user,\n                'Category': category,\n                'Period': period\n            })\n\nintensive_full_df = pd.DataFrame(intensive_full)\n\n# Merge with actual data\nintensive_final = intensive_full_df.merge(\n    intensive_agg,\n    on=['Survey ResponseID', 'Category', 'Period'],\n    how='left'\n)\n\n# Fill missing Total_Spend with 0\nintensive_final['Total_Spend'] = intensive_final['Total_Spend'].fillna(0)\n\nprint(f\"   After filling missing combinations: {len(intensive_final)}\")\nprint(f\"   Zero-spend records: {(intensive_final['Total_Spend'] == 0).sum()}\")\nprint(f\"   Non-zero spend records: {(intensive_final['Total_Spend'] > 0).sum()}\")\n\n# Save intensive margin data\nintensive_path = output_dir / 'user_category_period_aggregated_intensive.csv'\nintensive_final.to_csv(intensive_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {intensive_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# CREATE EXTENSIVE MARGIN DATA (Has_Purchase)\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Creating intensive margin aggregated data:\")\n\n# Aggregate total spend per user-category-period\nintensive_agg = target_purchases.groupby([\n    'Survey ResponseID',\n    'Category',\n    'Period'\n]).agg({\n    'Total_Spend': 'sum'\n}).reset_index()\n\nprint(f\"   Intensive margin records: {len(intensive_agg)}\")\nprint(f\"   Unique users: {intensive_agg['Survey ResponseID'].nunique()}\")\nprint(f\"   Unique categories: {intensive_agg['Category'].nunique()}\")\n\n# Fill in missing user-category-period combinations with 0 spend\n# First, create all possible combinations\nall_users = features_df['Survey ResponseID'].unique()\nall_periods = ['baseline', 'treatment']\n\n# Create full grid\nintensive_full = []\nfor user in all_users:\n    for category in target_categories:\n        for period in all_periods:\n            intensive_full.append({\n                'Survey ResponseID': user,\n                'Category': category,\n                'Period': period\n            })\n\nintensive_full_df = pd.DataFrame(intensive_full)\n\n# Merge with actual data\nintensive_final = intensive_full_df.merge(\n    intensive_agg,\n    on=['Survey ResponseID', 'Category', 'Period'],\n    how='left'\n)\n\n# Fill missing Total_Spend with 0\nintensive_final['Total_Spend'] = intensive_final['Total_Spend'].fillna(0)\n\nprint(f\"   After filling missing combinations: {len(intensive_final)}\")\nprint(f\"   Zero-spend records: {(intensive_final['Total_Spend'] == 0).sum()}\")\nprint(f\"   Non-zero spend records: {(intensive_final['Total_Spend'] > 0).sum()}\")\n\n# Save intensive margin data\nintensive_path = output_dir / 'user_category_period_aggregated_intensive.csv'\nintensive_final.to_csv(intensive_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {intensive_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# CREATE EXTENSIVE MARGIN DATA (Has_Purchase)\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n6. Creating extensive margin aggregated data:\")\n\n# Create binary indicator for whether user purchased in category-period\nextensive_agg = target_purchases.groupby([\n    'Survey ResponseID',\n    'Category',\n    'Period'\n]).size().reset_index(name='transaction_count')\n\nextensive_agg['Has_Purchase'] = 1\n\nprint(f\"   Extensive margin records (actual purchases): {len(extensive_agg)}\")\n\n# Merge with full grid\nextensive_final = intensive_full_df.merge(\n    extensive_agg[['Survey ResponseID', 'Category', 'Period', 'Has_Purchase']],\n    on=['Survey ResponseID', 'Category', 'Period'],\n    how='left'\n)\n\n# Fill missing Has_Purchase with 0\nextensive_final['Has_Purchase'] = extensive_final['Has_Purchase'].fillna(0).astype(int)\n\nprint(f\"   After filling missing combinations: {len(extensive_final)}\")\nprint(f\"   No purchase (0): {(extensive_final['Has_Purchase'] == 0).sum()}\")\nprint(f\"   Has purchase (1): {(extensive_final['Has_Purchase'] == 1).sum()}\")\n\n# Save extensive margin data\nextensive_path = output_dir / 'user_category_period_aggregated_extensive.csv'\nextensive_final.to_csv(extensive_path, index=False)\nprint(f\"\\n   ✓ Saved: {extensive_path}\")\n\n# ============================================================================\n# VERIFY DATA STRUCTURE\n# ============================================================================\nprint(\"\\n7. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /app/.claude/skills/did_causal_analysis\n\n---\nskillx:\n  name: did_causal_analysis\n  purpose: Analyze spending pattern changes using Difference-in-Differences causal inference to identify demographic drivers of category-level anomalies\n  scope_in:\n    - Causal analysis of trend anomalies with demographic features\n    - Identifying drivers of spending changes across treatment vs baseline periods\n    - DiD with both intensive margin (how much) and extensive margin (how many) estimation\n  scope_out:\n    - Simple descriptive statistics without causal inference\n    - Time-series forecasting without treatment/control comparison\n    - Single-period analysis without baseline-treatment structure\n  requires:\n    - Cleaned demographic data with numeric engineered features\n    - Transaction data aggregated to user-category-period level\n    - Clear baseline and treatment period definitions\n    - Anomaly detection results identifying target categories\n    - Python with pandas, statsmodels for DiD regression\n  preferred_tools:\n    - pandas for data manipulation and aggregation\n    - statsmodels OLS/WLS for DiD regression with p-values\n    - Standard statistical libraries (numpy, scipy)\n  risks:\n    - Confusing intensive (purchasers only) with extensive (all users) margins\n    - Including non-participants in intensive margin dilutes effects\n    - Not creating complete grid for extensive margin biases rates\n    - Using manual calculation loses p-value significance testing\n    - Wrong baseline period selection (e.g., 2019 instead of immediate pre-treatment)\n  examples:\n    - Analyzing March 2020 spending surge/slump with demographic drivers\n    - Comparing intensive (spending per buyer) vs extensive (adoption rate) effects\n    - Identifying top 3 features explaining behavioral changes\n\n# Guidance\n\n## DiD Methodology Core Concepts\n\n### Intensive Margin vs Extensive Margin\n\n**Intensive Margin** - How much behavior changed among participants:\n- **Question**: \"Did buyers spend MORE per purchase?\"\n- **Data**: Sparse - only users who made purchases (excludes non-buyers)\n- **Outcome**: Continuous (total spending per user-category-period)\n- **CRITICAL**: Do NOT include zeros for non-purchasers\n\n**Extensive Margin** - How many people changed behavior:\n- **Question**: \"Did MORE people start buying?\"\n- **Data**: Complete panel - ALL users × categories × periods\n- **Outcome**: Binary (0 = no purchase, 1 = made purchase)\n- **CRITICAL**: MUST include non-purchasers\n\n### Data Preparation\n\n**For Intensive Margin:**\n```python\n# Only aggregate actual transactions - do NOT create complete grid\nintensive_df = transactions.groupby(['user_id', 'category', 'period'])['spending'].sum().reset_index()\n# Result: Only rows where purchases occurred (sparse)\n```\n\n**For Extensive Margin:**\n```python\n# Create complete user × category × period grid\ncomplete_grid = pd.DataFrame(\n    list(product(all_users, target_categories, ['baseline', 'treatment'])),\n    columns=['user_id', 'category', 'period']\n)\n\n# Mark who purchased\npurchases_lookup = transactions[['user_id', 'category', 'period']].drop_duplicates()\npurchases_lookup['has_purchase'] = 1\n\nextensive_df = complete_grid.merge(purchases_lookup, how='left')\nextensive_df['has_purchase'] = extensive_df['has_purchase'].fillna(0).astype(int)\n```\n\n### Regression Methods\n\nDiD regression: `Y = α + βX + γPost + δ(X × Post) + ε`\n- Interaction coefficient δ is the DiD estimate for feature X\n- Use statsmodels OLS/WLS to get p-values\n\n**Multivariate Heterogeneous DiD**: All features simultaneously, controls for confounding (use when n_observations ≥ n_features × 10)\n\n**Univariate DiD**: Separate regression per feature, more robust with small samples\n\n## Output Requirements\n\nFor each category (top 10 surge, top 10 slump):\n- **Intensive margin**: Top 3 features sorted by DiD estimate strength\n  - Surge: descending (largest positive first)\n  - Slump: ascending (largest negative first)\n- **Extensive margin**: Top 3 features sorted by DiD estimate strength (same logic)\n- Each driver: feature name, did_estimate, p_value, method\n\n## Period Definition\n\n- **Baseline**: Immediate pre-treatment (e.g., Jan-Feb 2020) - NOT distant history\n- **Treatment**: Anomaly window (e.g., March 2020)\n\n# Execution Notes\n\n## Critical Distinctions\n\n1. **Intensive requires SPARSE data** (purchasers only) - including non-purchasers changes the question\n2. **Extensive requires COMPLETE panel** (all users) - missing non-purchasers biases rates\n3. **Filter to target categories BEFORE DiD** - only top-N anomalous categories\n4. **Use regression, not manual calculation** - to get p-values and significance\n\n## Common Mistakes\n\n- Creating complete grid for intensive → Wrong, dilutes effects\n- Only including purchasers for extensive → Wrong, can't measure adoption rates\n- Analyzing all categories instead of filtering → Wastes computation\n- Using 2019 as baseline instead of immediate pre-treatment → Weakens causal identification\n- Not sorting drivers by magnitude → Returns arbitrary features\n\n## Verification Steps\n\n1. Create treatment dummy (1 for treatment period, 0 for baseline)\n        data = data.copy()\n        data['Post'] = (data[period_col] == 'treatment').astype(int)\n\n        # Create interaction term\n        data['Feature_x_Post'] = data[feature_col] * data['Post']\n\n        # Prepare regression data\n        X = data[[feature_col, 'Post', 'Feature_x_Post']]\n        X = sm.add_constant(X)\n        y = data[outcome_col]\n\n        # Run OLS regression\n        model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()\n\n        # DiD estimate is the coefficient on the interaction term\n        did_estimate = model.params['Feature_x_Post']\n        p_value = model.pvalues['Feature_x_Post']\n\n        return did_estimate, p_value\n    except Exception as e:\n        return 0.0, 1.0\n\ndef run_multivariate_did(data, outcome_col, feature_cols, period_col='Period'):\n    \"\"\"\n    Run multivariate heterogeneous DiD with all features\n    Returns: dict of {feature: (did_estimate, p_value)}\n    \"\"\"\n    try:\n        data = data.copy()\n        data['Post'] = (data[period_col] == 'treatment').astype(int)\n\n        # Create interaction terms for all features\n        interaction_cols = []\n        for feat in feature_cols:\n            interaction_name = f'{feat}_x_Post'\n            data[interaction_name] = data[feat] * data['Post']\n            interaction_cols.append(interaction_name)\n\n        # Prepare regression: outcome ~ features + Post + (features × Post)\n        X_cols = feature_cols + ['Post'] + interaction_cols\n        X = data[X_cols]\n        X = sm.add_constant(X)\n        y = data[outcome_col]\n\n        # Run OLS regression\n        model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()\n\n        # Extract DiD estimates (coefficients on interaction terms)\n        results = {}\n        for feat, interaction_name in zip(feature_cols, interaction_cols):\n            if interaction_name in model.params.index:\n                results[feat] = (model.params[interaction_name], model.pvalues[interaction_name])\n            else:\n                results[feat] = (0.0, 1.0)\n\n        return results\n    except Exception as e:\n        return {feat: (0.0, 1.0) for feat in feature_cols}\n\ndef analyze_category_intensive(category, intensive_df, features_df, feature_cols):\n    \"\"\"\n    Analyze intensive margin for a category\n    Returns: list of top 3 drivers\n    \"\"\"\n    # Choose method based on sample size\n    if n_obs >= n_features * 10:\n        # Use multivariate DiD\n        results = run_multivariate_did(cat_data, 'Total_Spend', feature_cols)\n        method = \"Multivariate Heterogeneous DiD\"\n\n        # Convert to list\n        driver_list = [\n            {\n                'feature': feat,\n                'did_estimate': float(estimate),\n                'p_value': float(pval),\n                'method': method\n            }\n            for feat, (estimate, pval) in results.items()\n        ]\n    else:\n        # Use univariate DiD\n        method = \"Univariate DiD\"\n        driver_list = []\n\n        for feat in feature_cols:\n            estimate, pval = run_univariate_did(cat_data, 'Total_Spend', feat)\n            driver_list.append({\n                'feature': feat,\n                'did_estimate': float(estimate),\n                'p_value': float(pval),\n                'method': method\n            })\n\n    # Sort by absolute magnitude of DiD estimate\n    driver_list.sort(key=lambda x: abs(x['did_estimate']), reverse=True)\n\n    # Return top 3\n    return driver_list[:3]\n\ndef analyze_category_extensive(category, extensive_df, features_df, feature_cols):\n    \"\"\"\n    Analyze extensive margin for a category\n    Returns: list of top 3 drivers\n    \"\"\"\n    # Convert to list\n        driver_list = [\n            {\n                'feature': feat,\n                'did_estimate': float(estimate),\n                'p_value': float(pval),\n                'method': method\n            }\n            for feat, (estimate, pval) in results.items()\n        ]\n    else:\n        # Create treatment dummy (1 for treatment period, 0 for baseline)\n        data = data.copy()\n        data['Post'] = (data[period_col] == 'treatment').astype(int)\n\n        # Create interaction term\n        data['Feature_x_Post'] = data[feature_col] * data['Post']\n\n        # Prepare regression data\n        X = data[[feature_col, 'Post', 'Feature_x_Post']]\n        X = sm.add_constant(X)\n        y = data[outcome_col]\n\n        # Run OLS regression\n        model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()\n\n        # DiD estimate is the coefficient on the interaction term\n        did_estimate = model.params['Feature_x_Post']\n        p_value = model.pvalues['Feature_x_Post']\n\n        return did_estimate, p_value\n    except Exception as e:\n        return 0.0, 1.0\n\ndef run_multivariate_did(data, outcome_col, feature_cols, period_col='Period'):\n    \"\"\"\n    Run multivariate heterogeneous DiD with all features\n    Returns: dict of {feature: (did_estimate, p_value)}\n    \"\"\"\n    try:\n        data = data.copy()\n        data['Post'] = (data[period_col] == 'treatment').astype(int)\n\n        # Create interaction terms for all features\n        interaction_cols = []\n        for feat in feature_cols:\n            interaction_name = f'{feat}_x_Post'\n            data[interaction_name] = data[feat] * data['Post']\n            interaction_cols.append(interaction_name)\n\n        # Prepare regression: outcome ~ features + Post + (features × Post)\n        X_cols = feature_cols + ['Post'] + interaction_cols\n        X = data[X_cols]\n        X = sm.add_constant(X)\n        y = data[outcome_col]\n\n        # Run OLS regression\n        model = sm.OLS(y, X).fit()\n\n        # Extract DiD estimates (coefficients on interaction terms)\n        results = {}\n        for feat, interaction_name in zip(feature_cols, interaction_cols):\n            if interaction_name in model.params.index:\n                results[feat] = (model.params[interaction_name], model.pvalues[interaction_name])\n            else:\n                results[feat] = (0.0, 1.0)\n\n        return results\n    except Exception as e:\n        return {feat: (0.0, 1.0) for feat in feature_cols}\n\ndef analyze_category_intensive(category, intensive_df, features_df, feature_cols):\n    \"\"\"\n    Analyze intensive margin for a category\n    Returns: list of top 3 drivers\n    \"\"\"\n    # Choose method based on sample size\n    if n_obs >= n_features * 10:\n        # Use multivariate DiD\n        results = run_multivariate_did(cat_data, 'Total_Spend', feature_cols)\n        method = \"Multivariate Heterogeneous DiD\"\n\n        # Convert to list\n        driver_list = [\n            {\n                'feature': feat,\n                'did_estimate': float(estimate),\n                'p_value': float(pval),\n                'method': method\n            }\n            for feat, (estimate, pval) in results.items()\n        ]\n    else:\n        # Use univariate DiD\n        method = \"Univariate DiD\"\n        driver_list = []\n\n        for feat in feature_cols:\n            estimate, pval = run_univariate_did(cat_data, 'Total_Spend', feat)\n            driver_list.append({\n                'feature': feat,\n                'did_estimate': float(estimate),\n                'p_value': float(pval),\n                'method': method\n            })\n\n    # Sort by absolute magnitude of DiD estimate\n    driver_list.sort(key=lambda x: abs(x['did_estimate']), reverse=True)\n\n    # Return top 3\n    return driver_list[:3]\n\ndef analyze_category_extensive(category, extensive_df, features_df, feature_cols):\n    \"\"\"\n    Analyze extensive margin for a category\n    Returns: list of top 3 drivers\n    \"\"\"\n    #
